Our Government Proposes to Conclude a 34

Sino-Russian Non-Aggression Treaty to Prevent the Soviet Union from Selling the Chinese Eastern Railway 35

and Establishing Formal Relations with the Puppet State

(Moscow) The Foreign Affairs Committee has received from Ambassador Bogomolov to China the Chinese government's proposal

to negotiate and conclude a Sino-Soviet non-aggression treaty. The Chinese government's proposal is accompanied by "a draft treaty, divided into eleven articles, and also contains provisions for the conclusion of a mediation agreement. The articles of the draft, in addition to" the content of general non-aggression treaties, include a special article on the current situation in the Far East, requiring that both legally and in fact, any state created by a third country through acts of aggression must be refused recognition. This article gives the treaty a special quality, the purpose of which is clearly to prevent the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway and prevent the Soviet Union from establishing formal relations with "Manchukuo." As for other parts that are the same as ordinary non-aggression treaties, they include opposition to war and hostile acts, refusal to help a third country's acts of aggression, refusal to participate in agreements that undermine the other side's territorial integrity and political independence, and mutual non-interference in internal affairs, etc. (24th TASS dispatch)

Japanese Plan to Block the Joint Transport of the Chinese Eastern Railway and the Ussuri Railway 36

Soviet Russia Believes Japan's Sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway to Soviet Russia Violates the Sino-Soviet Agreement, Still No Reply 37

(Moscow) According to recent news obtained from here, the

terrifying state of the Chinese Eastern Railway remains unchanged. Manchurian and Japanese authorities continue to obstruct the normal operation of the railway through various means. Recently, there has been a new movement that threatens to further aggravate the situation. According to reliable sources, a meeting was recently held at the Japanese Embassy in Changchun, deciding to suspend the joint transportation of the Chinese Eastern Railway and the Ussuri Railway by the end of May. The purpose of this is twofold: first, to block all railway traffic to Vladivostok, diverting the original freight of the Chinese Eastern Railway to Dalian; and second, to undermine the operation of the Chinese Eastern Railway, thereby enhancing the Japanese position in negotiations to purchase the railway. Regarding the above news, the Soviet government gazette "Izvestia" commented today that although negotiations between Japan and the Soviet Union regarding the Chinese Eastern Railway are underway, and representatives of the Soviet Union, Japan, and Manchuria are also conducting negotiations in Harbin, aggressive elements in Manchuria continue their provocative activities to prevent the peaceful resolution of misunderstandings and conflicts arising from the railway. To achieve this goal, these provocateurs are creating new conflicts, keeping the relations between the two countries in a state of constant disputes. The obstruction of traffic in Vladivostok not only violates the Beijing and Shenyang agreements but also violates the agreement on the opening of the Chinese Eastern Railway and the Ussuri Railway. However, in order to avoid the accusation of violating the treaty, the Japanese in Changchun will disguise the next move to undermine the international railway agreement as a purely technical matter. However, if Japanese and Manchurian officials do not recognize the crudeness and provocative nature of this move and believe that it can reduce the price of purchasing the railway, then they are too naive." The newspaper concludes: "In our opinion, the main purpose of the Manchurian provocateurs is to obstruct, by all means, the negotiations to resolve all current disputes and the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway. However, if Tokyo also participates in this plan, then Japan's failure to respond to the Soviet Union's proposal to sell the Chinese Eastern Railway has an explanation." (TASS Dispatch, 24th)

The Color of the Han River Changes 41

Chaozhou and Meizhou Counties Report Droughts

(Shantou) In Chao'an, a rainbow circled the sun for half an hour. The

Han River turned red, and sand and mud boiled up, turbid like blood. From Zhu Nian Mountain to Jishui Pagoda near the city, people switched to drinking well water. The phenomenon lasted for twenty hours before disappearing. The river had changed color once in ancient times, which was a sign of a bad harvest year. Currently, Chaozhou and Meizhou counties are reporting droughts. (Special Dispatch, 24th)

The Disarmament Conference is in Progress 49

Britain Proposes a Consultation Pact 50

The United States Agrees to a Declaration Guaranteeing Joint Action Against Aggressor Nations Determined by Consultation 51

(Geneva) Today, British Foreign Secretary Simon presented a new draft of the Consultation

Pact in the General Disarmament Committee that can meet the attitude of the United States. It stipulates that in the event of a violation or endangerment of the Pact of Paris, regardless of whether it is the Council or the Assembly of the League of Nations or non-League members, they may propose that the Council or the Assembly of the League of Nations immediately consult with any signatory country on this matter. The draft declares that the purpose of the consultation is (1) to exchange views in order to maintain peace and avoid team conflicts if the Pact of Paris is at risk of being violated; (2) to mediate and restore peace in the event of a violation of the Pact of Paris; (3) if peace cannot be restored, to determine who is responsible among the countries involved. The draft finally declares that the aforementioned clauses in no way prejudice the rights or obligations of League members, nor do they conflict with or restrict the responsibilities and powers of the League Assembly or the Council. (National Telegram, 24th)

(Geneva) Today, the US representative Davis explained at the General Disarmament Committee meeting the United States' contribution to the issue of security.

He said that the United States will issue a separate declaration at the time of ratifying the Disarmament Convention, guaranteeing that in the event of mutual consultation among countries, an agreement is reached on joint action against aggressor nations, and the United States agrees with the document determining the aggressor nations, the United States will not take any action to undermine such joint action. If the activities of the American people tend to undermine such joint action, the US government will stop protecting them.

(National Telegram, 24th)

(Geneva) France's acceptance of the British disarmament plan is subject to strict conditions. Today,

the representatives attending the General Committee all expect that there is little hope for an early agreement on the reduction of armaments. According to the conditions for France's acceptance of the disarmament part of the British plan proposed by French representative Peng Gu, (1) strictly manage international armaments and absolutely prohibit private arms manufacturing; (2) all offensive weapons should be handed over to the League of Nations, and France does not agree to destroy them; (3) conclude several European mutual assistance pacts to provide France with appropriate security; (4) standardize all war equipment and troops. It is also heard that unless the French are completely satisfied with all their demands, they are not even willing to try to accept the British plan. Therefore, the representatives all frankly stated that the French demands will be a major obstacle to reaching an agreement.

However, according to the French opinion, the

arms that have already been manufactured should be handed over to the League of Nations for management, so that they may be used to stop major wars someday in the future. Why destroy them? In addition, other items are also necessary for French security. However, no matter what else, the prohibition of private arms manufacturing alone is enough to hinder the establishment of a disarmament agreement, because this matter will become an economic issue. Since the government will not be able to order from private companies in the future, it will have to manufacture itself. However, many countries will feel that it is difficult to complete the equipment for manufacturing military supplies in the near future. (National Telegram, 23rd)

(Geneva) The Disarmament Conference has encountered difficulties again as a result of French representative Peng Gu's speech today.

When discussing Article 22 concerning the destruction of tanks and land artillery, Peng Gu stated that the French government cannot comply with this unless the security and management and standardization of armaments requested by France have been fulfilled. German representative Nascheni then declared on the spot that Germany would have no choice but to withdraw its recognition of the disarmament plan. It is believed that British Foreign Secretary Simon will contact the French delegation in order to seek understanding. There was another unexpected event this afternoon. Turkish representative Rushdi Bei requested the abolition of the Straits clause in the Treaty of Versailles, saying that Turkey should have the right to rebuild the fortresses on the Bosphorus and Dardanelles straits and install heavy artillery. This issue may be studied by a committee composed of representatives of the Black Sea and Mediterranean countries and the United States and Japan. Peng Gu stated that the General Committee of the Disarmament Conference is not qualified to amend the treaty, but it was decided after public discussion to send the Turkish proposal to the various committees. (Reuters Dispatch, 23rd)

(Washington) Political circles here expressed the opinion that it is difficult for the United States to agree with

France's attitude towards disarmament expressed by French Foreign Minister Peng Gu in Geneva yesterday. Peng Gu announced that France opposes the destruction of aggressive war equipment and advocates that the League of Nations preserve it. (Reuters Dispatch, 24th)

(Berlin) German officials believe that US representative Davis's remarks in

Geneva yesterday were a step towards disarmament. German officials attach particular importance to the US representative's statement that countries with full armaments have an obligation to disarm so that they are equal to countries that have lifted their armaments. They said that this statement indicates that the United States has recognized the equal rights that Germany has requested, that is, to reduce armaments to the limits set by the Treaty of Versailles within the scope of general disarmament. France should now clearly indicate whether it really wants to reduce disarmament according to the British plan. (Reuters Dispatch, 23rd)

Poland and the Little Entente Still 52

Oppose the Four-Power Pact 53

Strenuously Consult with the French Government

(Geneva) Poland and the Little Entente (i.e., Yugoslavia,

Czechoslovakia, and Romania) are now very alarmed by the rumor that the Four-Power Pact between Britain, France, Italy, and Germany will be signed. Polish representatives stationed in Geneva and Paris have repeatedly held lengthy talks with French authorities on this matter. At the same time, Polish cabinet members also held a talk with the French ambassador in Warsaw yesterday. Representatives of the Little Entente are also making strenuous efforts in Paris on this matter. It is also heard that France is nervously consulting with Poland on one hand and contacting the Little Entente on the other. Once the Four-Power Pact is established, the policies of the Central European countries may change direction. According to a semi-official Warsaw statement, whether Poland is invited to join or not, Poland will definitely oppose any form of the Four-Power Pact. The general opinion in Warsaw is that the current form of the pact is a way to replace the principle of equality among nations with the principle of the superiority of a certain country. Poland is an autonomous group, and any treaty that Poland has not participated in the discussion and signed cannot bind Poland. (Reuters Dispatch, 24th)

(Paris) The French government has not yet received the new draft of the Four-Power Pact from Rome.

There are currently two issues that remain to be negotiated: one is the effective period of the pact. Germany advocates five years, while the other three countries advocate ten years. The other is the method of initiating treaty revisions. It seems that there is no final decision on the above two points. (Reuters Dispatch, 23rd)

(Paris) According to the Petit Parisien, French Foreign Minister

Peng Gu met with Italian representative Arazzi in Geneva at 8:00 PM last night. It is heard that Arazzi informed Peng Gu that Italy and Germany have both agreed to the memorandum submitted by France regarding the draft of the Four-Power Treaty and the various revisions requested by the French Foreign Ministry. On the same evening, Peng Gu also held talks with the foreign ministers of the Little Entente countries for several hours. The content of the talks is unknown. (Havas Dispatch, 24th)

Stabilizing International Exchange Rates 54

(New York) As rumors spread that the exchange rate of the US dollar against foreign currencies will be stabilized within

a week, the Federal Reserve Banks in this and eleven other districts suddenly established an open market for purchasing government bonds. Several prominent bankers and financial experts in New York said that this move is an improper procedure that will endanger the life of the entire government bond market. In the future, the reserve banks will either destroy the market or never be able to resell these government bonds. However, according to Treasury Secretary Woodin, the maximum amount of bonds purchased at this time will not exceed 25 million yuan. Woodin did not comment on the impact of this move, but the New York Stock Exchange believes that it is the government's first step towards real inflation. However, bankers have slightly different observations, believing that its inflationary component is not as large as the expansion of credit (i.e., lending). According to the purchase of government bonds or government debt and the debt of companies in which the government is a major shareholder, it is authorized by Congress, that is, stipulated in the Rural Relief Act. Today, the initial price of the yuan was already weak, and the news of inflation made the prices of securities and goods soar, because merchants all believe that the rumor of stabilizing exchange rates is reliable, and they also believe that the value of the gold yuan after stabilization will be slightly lower than the price in the past week. However, regarding immediate stabilization, it has not been confirmed in Washington or London. Only the major countries are trying to stabilize currency prices before the opening of the Economic Conference. As for Wall Street and financial experts, they mostly oppose the re-inflation of the gold yuan today, believing that the only safe way at present is to stop inflating currency and focus on inflating credit. (National News Agency Dispatch, 23rd)

Jiangxi Province Will Form Six Security Divisions 58

Specially Responsible for Protecting the Local Area

(Nanchang) In order to expand the people's self-defense forces, the Jiangxi Provincial Authorities

will establish six security divisions. In addition to the establishment of the first and second divisions immediately, four more divisions will be established. The organization of the security division is based on the security teams of each county, with every four counties being grouped into one division. If there are not enough people, they will be recruited separately. The funds will be the funds of the ten county teams. If there is not enough, the provincial treasury will subsidize them. The security division is specially responsible for protecting the local area. In addition to the security within the four counties, they must also assist in pursuing and suppressing bandits if there is a bandit alert in neighboring counties. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 24th)

Liu Zhenhua's Telegram States 59

His Opinions on Governing Anhui 60

(Nanchang) Anhui Chairman Liu Zhenhua recently replied in a telegram to the Anhui fellow-provincial association in Beijing, stating three points regarding his opinions on governing Anhui: (1) The 11th Route Army under his command is directly under the central government, and the funds are received by the central government. The deployment is presided over by the central government. No matter where they are stationed, they will never increase the burden on the people. (2) He has always advocated that financial revenue and expenditure should be appropriate and the use of funds should be transparent. (3) The members of the provincial government should be selected by the central government based on talent, regardless of provincial origin. Many Anhui elites participated this time. Finally, he said that Hua serves the country and always takes the interests of the people as the premise. In the future, he will continue to uphold the spirit of cooperation with the people, work diligently to govern, in order to live up to the expectations of the elders in Anhui. United States Senate Investigates Morgan Bank 101

Washington, 23rd (Reuters)—J. P. Morgan, president of the internationally renowned

Morgan Bank, was summoned to the Senate Securities Market Investigation Committee today. Accompanying him was his lawyer, John Davis, who once served as the Ambassador to the United Kingdom. The audience was large. Although the Senate committee room was spacious, it was still crowded, as this was unprecedented. The Morgan Company is a private enterprise, and as such, it is neither subject to the scrutiny of ordinary government banks nor required to publish a balance sheet to the public. The Senate committee has been sending personnel to investigate the company's books for months. According to Morgan, the company has a total of 250 million yuan in deposits and assets totaling 424 million yuan. Morgan stated that private banks are a benefit to the country, not a detriment. We have never been satisfied with merely abiding by the law of the land and have always sought to act in accordance with business regulations and to maintain the reputation passed down by our predecessors. The company's shareholders did not pay income tax in 1931 and 1932, and in 1930 they only paid 48,000 yuan in income tax. The company declared a loss of 21 million yuan as a result of its operations on January 12, 1931. The United States Internal Revenue Service has no objection to this report. Government experts are currently investigating the company's operations in 1932. Some members of the committee pointed out that private banks have too much power. Morgan replied that the power he has comes from the trust that the people have in his character and credit, but not because he simply possesses vast wealth. He has made mistakes, but they were errors of judgment rather than of principle. Although he does not approve of shareholders being dictators, he has had to do so because he is convinced that one of the duties of a private bank is to benefit the public in general and common affairs. The committee discovered that the bank had 167 employees who were managers. The committee decided to order the bank to hand over a list of shareholders, a list of customers with deposits of more than 100,000 yuan, a list of lending banks, and a list of favored customers.

Japanese Troops Pressing on Beiping and Tianjin, Peaceful Prospects Dim; 102

Three Routes Surround Beiping, Intending to Cut Off Communication Between Beiping and Tianjin, Each Route Directly Approaches Beiping, Only 50-60 Li Away

Inching Forward, Forcing Me to Accept a Treaty Under Duress

Beiping Special Dispatch: Recently, the attitude of the Japanese troops has become increasingly tough. In recent days, they have been advancing on Beiping and Tianjin according to their second-step plan. They are now proceeding in three routes, planning to surround Beiping. One route is advancing along the Pinggu Avenue from Miyun in a frontal attack, threatening the northern side of Beiping. The front line is only 80-90 li away from Beiping. Another route is advancing from Huairou towards Changping, preparing to bypass the Pinghan Railway and cut off Beiping's rear. A third route is crossing the North Canal from Yanjiao Town, advancing towards Tongzhou, threatening the eastern side of Beiping. Another route is attacking from Sanhe Xianghe, directly towards Langfang, intending to cut off communication between Beiping and Tianjin. Yesterday, Japanese soldiers were found near Changping to the north and in the vicinity of Sanhe. Yesterday afternoon, five or six hundred Japanese soldiers, eleven armored vehicles, eighteen artillery pieces, and three tanks were also seen in Yanjiao, west of the town on the banks of the Grand Canal, building a bridge, intending to cross the river. Today, the Japanese troops continue to advance. The front line is only 50-60 li away from Beiping. The Japanese troops in Tianjin are also pressing forward from the Yutian, Shizhi, Ninghe, and Tangfang lines. Before Huang Fu's trip north, there was considerable consultation with the other side regarding the security of Beiping and Tianjin. After arriving in Beiping, he discussed the matter with He Yingqin and other military commanders in the north and ordered the troops at the front to move successively to the planned defense line. It was originally planned to move the troops at the front in the shortest possible time and in the fastest possible manner. However, because of defense concerns, Song Zheyuan and Pang Bingxun and others could not come to Beiping for consultations as scheduled. At the same time, the Japanese troops were also pressing closer, resulting in a situation where the planned plan could not be fully complied with. Internal opinions on the Japanese side are extremely inconsistent. The soldiers at the front are extremely arrogant. Taking advantage of the transfer of our troops, they are actively pressing forward, intending to directly approach Beiping and Tianjin, forcing us to accept a treaty under duress. If they fail to achieve their wishes, they will launch a disturbance in Beiping and Tianjin, using Chinese traitors as internal collaborators to expand the scope and stir up chaos in the north. When Huang Fu first went north, the atmosphere of peace was strong. The Chinese traitors lurking in Tianjin incited the Japanese, eagerly seeking to harass. Although the Japanese are dissatisfied with what these people are doing, in a situation where their desires have not yet been fulfilled, they can also take advantage of their troubles to help them achieve their threatening conspiracy. The riots by plainclothes teams in Tianjin a few days ago occurred for this reason. However, the Japanese have not yet reached the point where they can fully exploit these people, so after the riots by the plainclothes teams, they were unable to expand the scope. In short, the various conspiracies and facilities of the Japanese troops against Beiping and Tianjin are all aimed at exhausting their ability to threaten, in order to achieve their great desires. As for the focus of the dispute between the two sides, there are roughly three points: (1) Our side takes the principle of no compromise and no seeking peace. Peace can only be achieved under mutual understanding, and the scope is limited to local areas. The Japanese side wants to take the opportunity to fulfill its desires and must at least tacitly acknowledge the existence of Manchukuo. (2) Our side advocates for indirect negotiations between private individuals, while the Japanese side wants to hold public negotiations. (3) Our side means that both sides must first cease military action. Now that our troops have been transferred, the Japanese side should also retreat. The Japanese side wants our troops to leave Beiping and Tianjin first before discussing other matters. The most difficult point is that the Japanese side is not only internally inconsistent and lacks credibility, but also the soldiers at the front are arrogant and unruly, and there is no one who can be responsible for presiding over matters. Often the morning's discussion changes in the evening, this person holds this view, and that person acts that way. There is nothing certain. Therefore, the situation has been changing unpredictably in recent days. The two basic conditions reported in the newspapers have not yet been formally put forward. What the future holds depends on the development of the situation in the next few days before it can be determined. Song Zheyuan, Pang Bingxun, and others returned to Beiping last night and went to Jurentang to meet He Yingqin. They had a secret talk until 2:00 AM this morning before leaving. This morning at 8:00 AM, Song and others went to Fengzeyuan to meet Huang Fu and talked for about an hour, then went to Jurentang to meet He again. Song's arrival is very important, and the outside world is paying close attention. Shang Zhen's appointment as governor of Henan has been internally decided. After the announcement, he will lead his three divisions and Gao Guizi's and Shen Ke's two divisions into Henan. Most of the remaining troops will move towards the Pinghan Railway. Transportation is currently quite difficult. A large army is still stationed in the suburbs of Beiping to prevent the Japanese army from invading. If the Japanese military are bent on having their way, then they will fight to the last ditch, even if it means betting everything. Residents outside the city are flocking to the city to take refuge, but order in the city is still quite stable. (22nd)

Full Text of Supreme Court's Verdict in the Hu Lifu Case 103

Han traitor Hu Lifu, dissatisfied with the Jiangsu High Court's verdict of December 12th, 1932,

sentenced to life imprisonment, appealed to the Supreme Court. The original prosecuting attorney, Zhu Wenzhuo, also appealed at the same time, believing that Hu Lifu's punishment was too lenient. The Supreme Court has now rendered its judgment, overturning the original verdict and sentencing him to death. The reasons for the verdict are briefly recorded at the end. Now that the full text of the judgment has been delivered, it is specially copied and recorded below. It is reported that as soon as the Supreme Court approves the Ministry of Judicial Administration's instruction to the Supreme Court Procuratorate to notify the Jiangsu High Court Procuratorate, the death sentence will be carried out immediately. The execution date will be issued in the near future.

Supreme Court Criminal Judgment No. 1632, Year 22 (Judgment) Appellant Jiangsu High Court Prosecutor, Appellant, i.e., Defendant Hu Lifu, male, 52 years old, native of Yongjia County, Zhejiang Province, residing at No. 105, Jinle Lane, Weihaiwei Road, Shanghai, businessman. The above-named appellants, in the case of the defendant's crime of treason, etc., dissatisfied with the first-instance judgment of the Jiangsu High Court on December 12th, 1932, have appealed. The court renders judgment as follows:

Ruling 104

The original judgment regarding the crime of serving in the enemy's army and the penalties

and execution of the sentence are all revoked. Hu Lifu is sentenced to death for serving in the enemy's army, and deprived of civil rights for life. Combined with the penalties imposed by the original judgment for the crimes of intending to profit from providing gambling venues and selling opium, and intending to profit from providing housing for people to use opium, the death penalty is carried out, and civil rights are deprived for life. The rest of the appeals are dismissed.

Facts 105

After January 28th, 1932, Hu Lifu

, when the Japanese army was severely disrupting Shanghai, and our 19th Route Army retreated to the second line of defense, Zhabei was occupied by the Japanese army. Hu Lifu then entrusted Engineer Washizaki, employed by Xiang Kaihecheng Nitric Acid Pharmaceutical Factory, to introduce him to the captain of the Japanese Fourth Battalion. Previously, the translators of the Japanese Fourth Battalion and others had formed the Jiangbei Headquarters to disrupt our army. After the Japanese army occupied Zhabei, they were eager to attack the Liuhuo and Taicang areas and were planning security in the rear, dissolving the headquarters. Coincidentally, Washizaki introduced Hu Lifu. Therefore, Translator Song and Captain Yamabana of the Japanese Army Headquarters ordered Hu Lifu to organize the Northern Citizens' Maintenance Association of the Northern City to replace the Jiangbei Headquarters. Hu Lifu was appointed as the chairman, and Yokota, a Japanese translator of the Fourth Battalion, was sent to the association. The association was divided into six groups: one was the General Affairs Group, with Washizaki and Yokota as directors; the second was the Finance Group, with Vice Chairman Wang Du concurrently serving as director; the third was the Patrol Group, with Chang Yuqing as director; the fourth was the Investigation Group, i.e., the Detective Section, with Yao Zhiduan as director; the fifth was the Transportation Group, with Cheng Hengchang as director; and the sixth was the Health Group, with Ding Qingyuan as director. There was also a Public Relations Group, which was presided over by Yan Dongyuan. There were about four or five hundred people in the association. The association was located in the Fourth District Police Station of Zabanzi Bridge. The affairs of the association were handled according to the instructions of the Japanese Fourth Battalion. The association fees still followed the methods of the Jiangbei Headquarters. All merchants and residents who transported goods out of Zhabei were required to have investigators from the association assess the price and collect a fee of 2%. After Hu Lifu signed and issued an exit permit, the Japanese army would check it and release them. It is estimated that from April 1st to April 10th of that year, more than 3,000 yuan was extorted. When the association existed, the Japanese army often went to inspect, and Yamabana personally praised Hu Lifu for maintaining it well. Later, after the League of Nations sent a telegram to the Japanese consul to inquire, the Japanese army claimed that it was a civilian organization and immediately ordered the association to be abolished. After the abolition, Hu Lifu reorganized the Jiuhe Company with Yokota and others, falsely claiming to be engaged in commerce. They opened gambling venues and opium dens in the company and sold opium. Among them, all affairs were still handled by Hu Lifu. It is estimated that within two weeks, more than 9,000 yuan was collected, half of which was taken away by Yokota, and the other half was used for company expenses. When the armistice was negotiated and the Japanese army withdrew from Zhabei, Hu Lifu, fearing punishment, hid in Washizaki's house. The Shanghai Municipal Government ordered his arrest many times without success. It was not until August 16th that Hu Lifu was lured to Xinya Restaurant on North Sichuan Road and arrested by detectives from the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau and handed over to the Jiangsu High Court Prosecutor for investigation and prosecution.

Reason 106

This case is divided into two parts for explanation as follows: (1) Regarding the organization

of the Maintenance Society, upon reviewing the files, the appellant Hu

Lifu stated in his confession at the Shanghai Public Security Bureau that, "I discussed it with Washizaki,

and he told me to come out. I thought this matter would definitely be opposed by the people and supervised by the government." He also said, "The Japanese Command knew that the Jiangbei Command was not doing a good job, so they wanted me to organize the Beishi (Northern Shanghai) Local Citizens' Maintenance Society." He also said, "I am the chairman, and there are six sections: Patrol Team, Investigation Team, Transportation Team, Finance Team, and General Affairs Team." "The General Affairs Team is headed by Washizaki Yokota." He also said, "Plainclothes patrol

officers maintain local order." He also said, "When merchants and residents move goods out of Zhabei, the society first sends investigators to estimate the value, and a tax of two yuan per hundred yuan of goods is collected, totaling more than three thousand yuan." He also said, "The transport permits at that time were issued by me." He also said, "From April 1st to the 10th, it lasted for ten days, and I handled everything." He also said, "At that time, foreigners sent telegrams to the International Federation, and the League of Nations sent telegrams to the Japanese consul to inquire about everything, and the American consul asked the Japanese consul whether it was organized by the Japanese, so the Japanese military headquarters ordered the cancellation of this Maintenance Society." During the investigation, he confessed that the Jiangbei Command was organized by the Japanese Fourth Battalion's interpreter's office. When we organized the Maintenance Society, the Jiangbei Command had already been disbanded." He also said, "The Japanese from the Fourth Battalion came to the Maintenance Society to inquire." He also said, "We cannot do things against the Fourth Battalion's consent." He also said, "There are several hundred members, and the content of the charter is to maintain public order..." (omission) "...added female inspectors." He also said, "At that time, the Japanese could not maintain it either, so they wanted me to come out and maintain it." He also said, "The Patrol Team is the police, and the Investigation Team is the detectives." He also said, "The Japanese army would let them pass if they saw the permit." He also said, "The Jiangbei Command had already done this before with the collection of cargo transport tax, and we are doing the same." He also said, "Washizaki went to smooth things over, and then sent Yokota. At that time, Yokota was already working as a translator in the Japanese Fourth Battalion. Yamazaki met me once and said that it was good that you came out to maintain it, and now the Jiangbei Command's reputation is too bad, so they want you to come out to maintain the place." In the original trial, he confessed that he told Washizaki, and Washizaki promised to tell the Japanese military commander that things would be successful by March 4th." He also said, "Yamazaki is the captain, and Takanatsu is the commander-in-chief." He also said, "The Japanese often came to check," etc. It is clear that the appellant has already explained how he entrusted Washizaki to smooth things over, organized the Beishi Local Citizens' Maintenance Society to replace the Jiangbei Command, how he was entrusted by the Japanese army, and was examined by them, how he divided into groups to handle affairs, and added female inspectors as well as police detectives, how he followed the Jiangbei Command's method of levying cargo transport taxes, how he helped to maintain the rear when the Japanese army could not maintain public order, and how he handled affairs according to the Japanese Fourth Battalion's wishes. All of these have been confessed frankly without hesitation. Referencing the investigation report obtained by the Shanghai Municipal Government, it is consistent. Although the appellant argued that the purpose of organizing the society was to handle charitable matters and had no political implications, and that he had reported it to the Municipal Government and was not entrusted by the Japanese army, etc., since the society had a chairman and vice-chairman, and was organized into six sections, and recruited police and hired detectives, how could it be said to have no political implications? Copying the Jiangbei Command's method of levying donations to harm the people, and setting up male and female inspectors to check entries and exits, how could it be entrusted as a charitable undertaking? Moreover, the so-called report, not only did the original trial send a letter to the Municipal Government to inquire, but it was replied that there was no such thing, and the original trial also reviewed the Municipal Government's files and found no documents of the appellant's report. It is extremely obvious that it is a cover-up. As for the layer of entrustment, the appellant only insisted on not admitting it because no entrustment documents were found. It should be known that the appellant's repeated confessions, such as "they wanted me to organize" and "I came out to maintain," etc., have already revealed the meaning of entrustment. Furthermore, the fact that the Japanese army would let them pass if they held the permit issued by the appellant, the society was questioned by the League of Nations, the Japanese military headquarters immediately ordered the cancellation, and the society's actions could not violate the Japanese Fourth Battalion's consent, and the Japanese often came to the society to inquire, etc., are sufficient to show that the power of existence, abolition, supervision was completely controlled by the Japanese army, and it is difficult to conceal that it was entrusted by the Japanese army. In addition, what the appellant has repeatedly argued is that he did not serve in the enemy army and did not harm the Republic of China. According to the meaning of serving, it refers to performing all affairs for the enemy army, regardless of whether it is participating in the enemy army's strategy or engaging in other miscellaneous affairs, etc. The appellant, when Zhabei was occupied by the Japanese army, was entrusted by the Japanese army and openly organized an illegal organization within its occupied area, and called on as many as four or five hundred followers to engage in detective inspections and levy taxes on the transport of goods, to maintain the rear order for the enemy, so that its troops invading Liuhe and Taicang could be fearless and devote all their efforts to advance to the front line, which increased the danger of the National Army resisting the enemy. If this is not called serving, what is called serving? If this is not called harming the Republic of China, what is called harming? Based on this, the original judgment determined that the appellant constituted the crime of Article 109, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law and Article 6 of the Emergency Law for Punishing Acts Endangering the Republic of China. According to Article 74 of the Criminal Law, the sentence was determined according to Article 109, Paragraph 1, which is not illegal. The appellant's appeal is not reasonable. However, the appellant has witnessed the fierce resistance of the National Army and the tragic attack on Beishi, but when the enemy army could not maintain the rear order, he entrusted someone to introduce him to the enemy and willingly served for them. Judging from the above situation, it is really unforgivable. The prosecutor's appeal stated that the defendant, i.e., the appellant, served as the chairman of the society, and the circumstances of the crime cannot be said to be insignificant. The original judgment only sentenced him to life imprisonment, and the sentencing was somewhat inappropriate, etc., which is hard to say without reason. (2) Regarding the organization of the company, after reviewing the files, the appellant Hu Lifu confessed at the Shanghai Public Security Bureau that after we retreated to Linping Road on April 11th, the economy was extremely panicked. At that time, I wanted to organize the Jiuhe Company..." (omission) "...The Japanese Yokota came up with the idea of opening gambling, selling cigarettes, and selling soil," etc. He also said, "I am responsible for it." He also said, "After two weeks, a total of more than nine thousand yuan was collected. Yokota took half, and the remaining half was used for the expenses of the Jiuhe Company," etc. It is clear that the appellant already admitted in detail that after the Citizens' Maintenance Society was disbanded, he intended to organize the Jiuhe Company, intending to make profits, and that gambling, selling cigarettes, and selling soil were handled by him within the company. The verification is still consistent with the investigation report obtained by the Shanghai Municipal Government. Although the appellant argued that the confessions made in the Public Security Bureau were due to torture, etc., it is only empty words and no evidence was presented, intending to overturn it, which is not credible. The original judgment therefore determined that the appellant violated Article 280 of the Criminal Law, sentenced him to two years of imprisonment and a fine of one thousand yuan, the crime of Article 6 of the Anti-Smoking Law, sentenced him to two years of imprisonment and a fine of one thousand yuan, and the crime of Article 10 of the Anti-Smoking Law, sentenced him to one year of imprisonment. The rule of evidence is not inappropriate. The appellant's appeal is still hard to say reasonable. Based on the above arguments, according to Article 409, Paragraph 1, Article 410, Paragraph 1, Item 1 of the Criminal Procedure Law, Article 41 of the Criminal Law, Article 109, Paragraph 1, Article 6 and Article 10 of the Emergency Law for Punishing Acts Endangering the Republic of China, Article 74, Article 120, Article 57, Paragraph 3, Article 70, Item 1 of the Criminal Law, and Article 408, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Procedure Law, the judgment is as stated in the main text.

The Control Yuan impeaches Chen Weizhou, the salt transport commissioner of Guangdong and Guangxi 107

Beijing News, Control Yuan member Jie Fu said that Wang Jiading, the former director of the Hunan Salt Transport Bureau,

and Chen Weizhou, the current salt transport commissioner of Guangdong and Guangxi, violated the salt law, harmed the country and the people, and specially filed an impeachment with the Control Yuan. After being submitted for review and established, it was transferred to the Central Public Disciplinary Committee for disciplinary action. Now, the full text of the impeachment and review report is recorded in detail below.

Original text of impeachment 108

For the matter of Guangdong salt being transported and sold to Hunan through bribery and illegal means,

specifically raise an impeachment case. Citizens' representatives Tang Jian and Xiao Du in Hunan

and various public organizations in Lian County, Guangdong, accused Chen Weizhou, the Guangdong salt transport commissioner,

of specially allowing Taili Heki Company to transport Guangdong salt to Hunan and to handle the sale of local salt in six counties in northern Guangdong. At the same time, the issuance of transport licenses to free salt merchants was stopped, and Wang Jiading, the former director of the Hunan Salt Transport Bureau, and Taili Heki Company signed a covenant, allowing only one company to transport and sell, and falsely claiming that they had accommodated all merchants and had the Ministry of Finance approve a trial run, accepted bribes, violated the law, and harmed the people, and vowed to oppose it, etc. It is found that the salt affairs in various places in our country, such as Lianghuai, Fujian, Zhejiang, and Shanxi, etc., since the implementation of commercial sales, have resulted in monopolies, causing numerous malpractices, raising prices, and mixing in mud and sand. On the one hand, it deprives the people of the freedom to purchase, causing them to eat expensive and inferior salt. On the other hand, it causes smuggled salt to flood the market, and the state's tax revenue is also reduced, resulting in the failure of salt administration, which is irreversible. Nothing is more serious than this, which harms the country from above and harms the people from below. From the former Qing Dynasty to the Republic of China, people of insight in the government and the public have advocated reform, but they have been dismissed by wealthy merchants who bribed officials. The Legislative Yuan, ignoring everything, resolved the new salt law, which clearly states in the first article of the first chapter that salt should be taxed on site and that people should be free to buy and sell, and no one should be allowed to monopolize it. It has been promulgated by the National Government and resolved by the National Assembly to implement it within a time limit. According to the latest report from the Salt Affairs Audit General Office, it is said that the new salt law of free buying and selling is difficult to achieve overnight nationwide, but efforts should be made to build warehouses and strictly organize field police to prepare for implementation. Now that it has been opened, it has reached more than half of the total, etc. Breaking the monopoly system is the fundamental spirit of the new salt law, and gradually restoring the people's freedom to buy and sell is the only policy for promoting salt administration. If it was originally free trade, but now it is packaged and sold by merchants, it is a reversal and the greatest crime of undermining the salt law. It is found that Guangdong salt has been sold to Hunan, and historically, no matter where the merchants are from, once they pay taxes and obtain a license from the Guangdong Transport Commissioner's Office, they can distribute salt for purchase and sale and sell it freely. The price is lower than Huai salt, and the porters and laborers in dozens of counties in Hunan carry local goods to exchange for Guangdong salt and return, making the trade between Hunan and Guangdong increasingly developed, with an annual amount of tens of millions. Not only is the social economy invigorated, but the state's tax revenue is also increased. It has been implemented for decades, and both the upper and lower levels are convenient. As early as 1929, Taili Heki Company, a Guangdong merchant, came to Hunan to promote package sales. According to Hu Xingchi, the director of the Transport Bureau at that time, the company bribed 200,000 yuan and asked for package transport, but because it would harm the people of Hunan too much, he refused to do it. Li Fengyao, who succeeded him, also did the same. Bin Bucheng, the former president of Hunan University, also exposed the matter in the Changsha Pili newspaper. What he said was true, and no one denied it. When Wang Jiading became the director, he was blinded by greed and signed the so-called 19 Articles of Covenant for Package Transport with the company. He did not submit it to the Ministry of Finance for instructions and approval, but instead, with the strength of the local officials, he submitted it to the provincial government for deliberation and approval. He Jian, the chairman of the provincial government, consulted the Ministry of Finance for approval to open it. On February 3, 1931, the Ministry of Finance replied to the Hunan Provincial Government, saying that the package merchant system has more disadvantages than advantages and has long been criticized by the world. The salt affairs in various places that were originally handled by package merchants are being reformed. It is not appropriate for places that are not package merchants to implement package merchants again, which would cause malpractices and leave a bad name, etc. It can be seen that the Ministry of Finance is determined to reform the salt administration and is unwilling to accommodate local officials in order to violate the law and harm the people. Later, the Hunan provincial authorities repeatedly used the pretext of urgent military expenses to coerce and repeatedly telegraphed for approval, but the Ministry of Finance still attached the condition of accommodating all transport merchants so that they would not lose their jobs, and it can be seen that they could not bear to ignore public opinion. However, the Hunan salt affairs authorities colluded with Chen Weizhou, the salt transport commissioner of Guangdong and Guangxi, and falsely reported that the company had accommodated 80% of the salt merchants, and then lied to the Ministry of Finance, and it was approved on July 7, 1932, to temporarily conduct a trial run. Chen Weizhou, the transport commissioner of Guangdong and Guangxi, approved the company to start early on November 1 and to bring local salt from six counties in northern Guangdong to Hunan for sale. At the same time, the transport licenses of the respective salt merchants were all stopped. Thus, this illegal and harmful package merchant system was finally realized, and all the citizens on the border of Hunan, Guangdong, and Guangxi rose up in opposition, and letters and telegrams were exchanged, but to no avail. After the Guangdong salt was monopolized by the company for sale, the salt stores with eight openings would be seen to close down at the same time, and all the merchants would lose their jobs, and millions of coolies and porters would have no way to make a living and would take risks. The price of Hunan salt is now raised by 2 yuan, 8 dimes, and 2 cents of small silver. In the future, the monopoly position will become increasingly stable, and it can be asserted that they will increase and mix it arbitrarily, even more than Huai salt. Then the entire population of more than 30 counties in southern Hunan will eat inferior and expensive salt, and its impact on livelihoods is not shallow. Unexpectedly, at a time when the upper and lower levels are advocating reform of the salt administration, such a bad policy has appeared. Isn't it strange? Salt tax is a central tax revenue. Recently, the surcharges in various provinces have also been unified under the central government. Then the reform of the salt system should be completely dominated by the Ministry of Finance. How can it be submitted to the provincial government for deliberation and approval? It can be seen that they are deliberately undermining the central salt administration. It can be seen that the responsible personnel of Hunan and Guangdong salt affairs, such as Wang Jiading, the former director of the Hunan Salt Transport Bureau, and Chen Weizhou, the current salt transport commissioner of Guangdong and Guangxi, accepted bribes, violated the law, and harmed the people. The evidence is conclusive, and they are guilty and cannot be pardoned. An impeachment should be filed according to law, and the National Government should be requested to take urgent relief measures, and the Ministry of Finance should be strictly ordered to revoke the order to allow Taili Heki Company to conduct a trial run of package transport and sale of Guangdong salt to Hunan, in order to maintain the rule of law and benefit the people's livelihood. Whether it is appropriate, please submit it to the president for review and implementation. Control Yuan member Luo Jiefu, April 15.

Review report 109

For the matter of reporting, the case was assigned to Luo Jiefu

Member Luo Jiefu impeached Wang Jiading, the former director of the Hunan Salt Transport Bureau,

and Chen Weizhou, the current salt transport commissioner of Guangdong and Guangxi, etc. for violating the salt law, harming the country and the people.

After joint review, it was agreed that the freedom to sell salt is stipulated by the new salt law. In places that were originally packaged by merchants, efforts should be made to reform. In places that have always been free, package merchants should not be allowed again. However, Wang Jiading, the director of the Hunan Salt Transport Bureau, and Chen Weizhou, the salt transport commissioner of Guangdong and Guangxi, were greedy for bribes and disregarded the people's livelihood. In six counties in Hunan, which have always been free to sell salt, Taili Heki Company was allowed to be the only one to sell Guangdong salt. It is undeniable that they violated the law and harmed the people. The director and transport commissioner should be handed over for disciplinary action according to law, and the Executive Yuan should be consulted to order the relevant agencies to cancel the package merchant method of Taili Heki Company in order to maintain the salt law and value the people's livelihood. This report is hereby submitted, and it is hoped that the president will review and implement it. Salt Affairs Committee members Zhou Lisheng, Zhang Hualan, and Yu Hongqi, April 24 (Riri News Agency).

Labor unrest occurs in Wuhan yarn factory 110

Many yarn factories have successively reduced working hours. Zhenhuan Yarn Factory announced its closure, and thousands of workers petitioned for resumption of work.

Hankou correspondence, recently, the number of unemployed people in Wuhan is over 100,000.

Those who are fortunate enough to find a job, such as dockers and rickshaw pullers, etc., are hired at reduced prices. They work hard all day but can hardly get enough to eat. Only factory workers have a fixed income and barely maintain their lives. Among the factories, yarn factories occupy an important position. The larger ones are Taian Yarn Factory, run by the Japanese, and Xin Xin Yarn Factory, Yuhua Yarn Factory, Zhenhuan Yarn Factory, First Yarn Factory, and Minsheng Yarn Factory, run by the Chinese. On March 28 this year, Taian Yarn Factory announced its closure, and the remaining workers suddenly became unemployed. On the 29th, Xin Xin Yarn Factory unexpectedly caught fire again, and a total of 4,000 workers lost their jobs. Half a million laborers had nowhere to go, and a wave of reduced working hours broke out in various factories. Minsheng Yarn Factory in Wuchang took the lead in implementing it, resulting in the tragic incident of soldiers and police shooting workers on April 30. Subsequently, Zhenhuan Yarn Factory and First Yarn Factory continued to reduce working hours. Under the mediation of the authorities, the workers reluctantly complied. The Minsheng incident was also resolved peacefully. The garrison headquarters believed that the situation was serious and that communist elements might take the opportunity to infiltrate and instigate unrest. It advised various factories to take the overall situation into consideration and maintain the status quo for at least May to ensure security. However, various factories claimed that their business was not prosperous. Only Yuhua Factory did not reduce working hours. After the wave of reduced working hours came to an end, Zhenhuan Yarn Factory suddenly announced its closure on the 22nd, and labor-capital disputes could not avoid expanding. The factory's capital has always been known to be abundant, and it is independently operated by Liu Huchen, the richest man in Wuchang. For more than ten years, its business has been quite good. After implementing reduced working hours and reduced wages this time, it still felt that the turnover was not working. On the 21st, Xu Shunwu, the manager of the factory, announced that the factory would be closed the next day to clear the accounts. On the one hand, he reported to the military and political authorities for protection, and on the other hand, he negotiated with the person in charge of the labor union. The labor union stated that the factory should maintain operations until the workers agreed, in order to comply with the spirit of labor-capital coordination. If the request was not accepted and operations were suspended abruptly, the factory should be responsible for any incidents that occurred. On the 22nd, the factory actually closed down and requested a large number of armed soldiers and police to suppress it. The workers suddenly lost their source of income and elected representatives Jia Kun, Deng Zhanyuan, Chen Laoda, etc., more than 50 people, to petition the provincial party headquarters, the provincial government, and the garrison headquarters, requesting that they be ordered to resume work. The Wuchang Textile Labor Union also urgently reported to the party, government, and military authorities, requesting that they take measures to provide relief, stating that "Although it is a fact that Zhenhuan Company's goods are sluggish, the workers still worked hard after the implementation of reduced working hours in order to maintain their lives. Unexpectedly, the company disregarded the overall situation and wanted to use the pretext of losses to close down, which is too much oppression. Among the yarn factories in Wuchang with abundant capital, Yuhua is the most, Zhenhuan is the second, and First Yarn and Minsheng are the next. Yuhua has not reduced working hours so far. Zhenhuan, First Yarn, and Minsheng have all implemented reduced working hours. First Yarn and Minsheng can continue to operate, and Xia Huan should not be unable to support it. It is really no different from putting thousands of our workers to death. In the face of the urgent foreign insults, the red disaster has not been cleared, and it is another eventful May. If thousands of workers are unemployed once, I am afraid that reactionary elements will take the opportunity to incite and endanger the local area." The factory has about 3,000 workers. Together with Taian and Xin Xin factories, the number of unemployed workers reaches 7,000 to 8,000. (According to Taian and Xin Xin,

Although the unemployed workers have been given relief, the number is very small.) It is a serious social problem in Wuhan. If First Yarn Factory and Minsheng Yarn Factory follow suit and close down again, the labor unrest will be even easier to expand. (22nd)

Cultural Relics Unearthed in Ling County 111

Buddhist relics are extremely valuable ancient artifacts have been transported to Jinan Library

Jinan correspondence, Song Dynasty buildings were discovered in Ling County, northern Shandong, last month,

and many ancient artifacts were obtained. The provincial government ordered the county to transport the ancient artifacts to Jinan for preservation. The ancient artifacts were transported to Jinan the day before yesterday. The provincial library was ordered by the provincial government to transport the ancient artifacts to the library for preservation today. A reporter visited and saw six ancient bronze mirrors, sixteen copper coins, one silver coin, one silver monk hat, two stone tablets, one stone coffin, and

a package of silver pieces (with patterns), and a small box of stones the size of beans, which are Buddhist relics, all obtained from the coffin. According to Wang Xiantang, the librarian, the ancient mirrors and ancient coins are not very important, but the stone coffin has research value. Because the discovery of stone coffins is not new, and there are also stone coffins from the Han Dynasty, but there are not many with text and paintings. This coffin has both words and paintings, which can be used to study the styles of stone coffins in the Song Dynasty, so it is quite valuable. The reporter witnessed that the coffin was about two feet long, one foot wide, and one foot deep, with one end large and one end small. Five monks were carved on each of the two sides, and two people were carved on the large end. It is not known what the intention was. Each wore a pointed hat, and the patterns were all raised, about one inch high. The words "Great Song Huangyou" were carved on the coffin lid. The style of the writing was ancient. The ancient bronze coins had the years of Xiangfu and Qingli. The silver coin was very thin and had the words "The world is peaceful and the people are safe" on it. The picture gallery has been properly preserved now.

The small stones in the stone coffin, like beads, are the only Buddhist relics. They originally appeared in the incense burner of Qianming Temple in Qihe Town, Changqing County, various states (the place where the ancient artifacts were discovered in Ling County). The local people liked to make offerings and raised funds to build a silver box to hold them. The box has been crushed (referring to the crushed silver pieces in the coffin). The small Buddha statues in the coffin are the decorations on the box, and there is also a hat top, which is the top of the lid. The box was placed in a stone coffin. The coffin and the stone tablet are carved with the scene of the relics coming out of the furnace. At that time, a kiosk was built for offering sacrifices. Later, it was submerged in the soil and only unearthed today after more than 800 years. It is a unique discovery in archeology and is of great value. Unfortunately, the inscription on the tablet is blurred. (23rd)

Letter 112

Letter from the Supervisor and Commissioner of the Second District of Hubei 113

To the Editor: Recently, I read in your newspaper's May 12 and 27 issues about the resolutions of the support conference after the Xin Renhe Wheel disaster to present the party and government agencies to arrest the murderer and bring him to justice. My name is mentioned in it, which is very surprising. Since I was appointed as the Administrative Supervisor and Commissioner of the Second District of Hubei by General Commander Chiang last September, I have been busy with military affairs and government affairs. Since taking office, I have not left my post and have no spare time to engage in shipping in Shanghai. Whether there is another person with the same name as me is something I could have ignored. However, since the conference claims to be organized by the fellow villagers' associations of Daye and other counties, I should have heard of it since I am stationed in Daye. There must be a misunderstanding, or there is another purpose. I cannot but state the facts and write to your newspaper for correction. I hereby inform you and wish you good health. Sincerely, Tang Ken, Administrative Supervisor and Commissioner of the Second District of Hubei, Shanghai Shen Bao. May 22.

Wuxi 116

Arson Attempt Due to Failed Extortion

In Zhang Huaili area of the Third District (Yangming Township) of the county,

a villager named Zhang Dalin had saved some money and was building several new houses. Before the completion of the construction, he was targeted by bandits. Two weeks ago,

he suddenly received a threatening letter from bandits identifying themselves as the Righteous and Brave Corps. The letter vaguely stated that the corps was experiencing financial difficulties and needed to "borrow" one hundred silver dollars, which should be delivered to the paper basket at the back gate of the private Tang Family Elementary School near Tang Lane by a certain date. Dalin disregarded the letter. A few days later, he received a second letter. Dalin still ignored it. Then, he received a third letter, with more serious language, stating that if he did not comply, they would set fire to the new houses. Dalin managed to gather thirty silver dollars and went to the agreed location the day before yesterday evening. Because there were many passersby, he stood by the roadside to observe. He saw a middle-aged man wearing black clothes and pants, carrying a black robe, reaching into the paper basket. The bandit, failing to find the money, walked eastward towards North Bridge in disappointment. Dalin returned home immediately. The back door suddenly caught fire late yesterday evening. Fortunately, a carpenter noticed it and extinguished the fire, preventing a major disaster. He has reported the situation to the First Branch Office of the Eighth Public Security Bureau for the arrest of the bandits.

Changzhou 120

Young Woman Hangs Herself

Wu Weichuan, residing at No. 7 Zhoujia Lane in the city, originally from Suzhou, had a daughter named Xiulin, 17

years old. Around 9:00 a.m. on the 23rd, the family went to relatives for business, leaving Xiulin alone at home. She changed into newly made clothes, closed the front and back doors, and hanged herself with a hemp rope. When her sister-in-law returned home and knocked on the door, it was tightly shut. Realizing something was wrong, she had a neighbor climb over the roof and enter the room. They found her hanging and took her down to try to save her, but it was too late. As for the reason for her suicide, some say she was worried about national affairs, while others say she had other secrets. The rumors vary, and the truth is unknown.

Strange Brick-Throwing Incident Near Yumei Bridge 121

A strange incident has occurred recently near Yumei Bridge inside the Xiaobeimen of this county,

namely, someone throws bricks and stones every night. Initially, it was just local gossip, but now it has caused a citywide sensation. People gather to watch every night, and the police have been ordered to investigate. The brick-throwing was even more severe the day before yesterday, with many people being hit by stones and suffering head injuries. The number of onlookers was even greater than before. Some say the bricks and stones were thrown from an empty house behind the nunnery, while others say they were thrown from a newly built house nearby. However, after searching everywhere, no trace was found. It is all being passed off as a strange occurrence.

Nantong 122

Capture of the Bandit Leader of Haimen

The bandit leader of Haimen, Sha Xiaosan, has committed many atrocities.

Chairman Chiang ordered the Jiangsu Provincial Government to arrest him, and

Chairman Gu secretly telegraphed Commissioner Ye of the Seventh Administrative District of Nantong to handle the arrest. The Sha bandit has been captured by the Magistrate of Haimen County and will be brought to Nantong for interrogation in the coming days.

Dasheng Factory to Resume Work Soon 123

The labor unrest at the Dasheng Cotton Mill has subsided, and work will resume soon. The Chairman of the Board of Directors of the factory,

Zhang Xiaoruo, telegraphed local groups, saying that Manager Li was appointed by the founder, Mr. Zese, and the board knew of his dedication to Mr. Zese's vision. Therefore, they entrusted him with reforming the factory affairs. All contracts with creditor groups and silver groups were established by the board, with clear boundaries. Outsiders, unaware of the truth, had misunderstandings, leading to this labor unrest. Now that the local community and workers have reached an understanding, as long as the factory operations can proceed without hindrance, the manager does not care about praise or blame. Xiaoruo and others have urged him to go to the factory to start work immediately, hoping to announce this to reassure the people.

Jiaxing 124

Jailer Accused of Being Reactionary

Yang Ziqing, a guard at the Third Prison of Jiaxing, was

secretly reported to the province for colluding with certain people in

organizing a reactionary organization in a thatched house near the Xiulun Silk Factory outside the South Gate on a certain day and planning a riot on May 18. The High Court secretly telegraphed the Jiaxing Branch Court to arrest him. Prosecutor Wang led the police to detain the prison guard Yang Ziqing and went to the thatched house to arrest Yang Jingshan, a farmer from Wenzhou. After interrogation revealed no reactionary connections, he was released on bail. Yang Ziqing was sent for trial, and the remaining suspects named in the secret report are currently under investigation.

Hangzhou 125

Zhejiang Province Unable to Repay Principal of Silk Industry Relief Bonds

The Zhejiang Provincial Government received an order from the Executive Yuan to issue

two million yuan of silk industry public bonds, which were sealed and not issued in the 20th year of the Republic, to provide relief to the silk industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. The Ministry of Finance would pay the interest, and the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces would be responsible for repaying the principal. The provincial government was ordered to quickly plan and implement the order. After receiving the telegram, the provincial government believed that with the silk industry declining daily and suffering a setback, issuing two million yuan of public bonds, no matter what, would be insufficient to cover expenses given the current situation. They requested that the previous plan of the Ministry of Industry to issue five million yuan be followed to provide relief. Furthermore, the province's rural villages are facing economic bankruptcy and financial exhaustion, and they are unable to bear the burden of repaying the principal of the public bonds. They requested that the Ministry of Finance be responsible for raising the necessary funds.

Ningbo 126

Sinking of the Fuhai Patrol Ship

The

Fujii patrol ship, belonging to the Fisheries Improvement Committee of the Jiangsu and Zhejiang region, was tasked with escorting the Jianbang small fishing boat to

sea for fishing. On the morning of the 20th, it departed from Jiamen and sailed to the waters of Banzidong, Putuo. A hole was discovered at the bottom of the ship, and seawater was seeping in. It urgently sailed to the beach of Lujiazhai to run aground. All valuable items inside the ship were removed. The empty ship was anchored on the beach. Unexpectedly, at noon that day, the tide rose sharply, and the ship broke its anchor and was swept away by the waves, sinking immediately. Fortunately, the important machinery of the ship had already been removed, so the loss was minimal.
